# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Java Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern in Kafka

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle: the Lifecycle interface (or equivalent), the service startup ordering, and the coordinated shutdown sequence that ensures dependent services stop in reverse order.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [

  ],

    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

68-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Apache Kafka codebase and created a comprehensive answer documenting the Java service initialization lifecycle pattern.

## Summary

I've identified and documented the Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle pattern in Apache Kafka with:

**Key Findings:**

1. **Core Architecture**: The `KafkaRaftServer` acts as the main orchestrator, managing both broker and controller components with careful startup/shutdown ordering.

2. **Broker Service Lifecycle** (`BrokerServer`): Implements sophisticated startup with 8 major initialization phases, and a reverse-order shutdown that carefully manages 11 phases of cleanup.

3. **Critical Pattern**: The scheduler shuts down early during broker shutdown to prevent background tasks from accessing resources being closed.

4. **Service Interfaces**: Multiple components implement the basic start/stop lifecycle:
   - `Scheduler` (startup/shutdown)
   - `GroupCoordinator` (startup/shutdown)
   - `ShareCoordinator` (startup/shutdown)
   - `Herder` (start/stop)
   - `ConfigBackingStore`, `StatusBackingStore`, `OffsetBackingStore` (start/stop)
   - `Task` (start/stop)

5. **Dependency Ordering**: Services start in forward dependency order and stop in reverse order, with extensive use of `CompletableFuture` for coordinating async initialization.

The answer is available at `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed information about all files, symbols, initialization chains, and a comprehensive narrative explaining the lifecycle patterns.

In startup(), the controller starts first before the broker (lines 90-98), and in shutdown(), the broker shuts down first before the controller (lines 100-107). This ordering ensures that the controller remains available for broker shutdown operations.\\n\\n## Broker Service Lifecycle\\n\\nThe BrokerServer (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala) implements the complex startup() method (line 189) that manages the initialization of numerous dependent services:\\n\\n1. **Scheduler Initialization** (line 204-205): The KafkaScheduler is created and started early to support all background tasks\\n2. **Socket Server Setup** (line 275-281): Network infrastructure initialization\\n3. **Metadata Cache Creation** (line 212): Core metadata caching\\n4. **Log Manager Initialization** (line 216-222): Log storage management\\n5. **Lifecycle Manager Creation** (line 224-228): Broker state tracking\\n6. **Coordinator Initialization** (lines 376-398): Group, share, and transaction coordinators\\n7. **Replica Manager Setup** (lines 345-364): Replication management\\n8. **Socket Server Enablement** (line 587): Final network activation\\n\\nThe shutdown() method (line 729) implements reverse dependency order:\\n1. Lifecycle manager begins shutdown/controlled shutdown (lines 735-753)\\n2. Socket server stops accepting requests (line 758)\\n3. Metadata publishers are removed (lines 760-761)\\n4. Quota managers shutdown (line 815-816)\\n10. Socket server shutdown (line 818-819)\\n11. Lifecycle manager begins shutdown/controlled shutdown (lines 735-753)\\n2. Socket server stops accepting requests (line 758)\\n3. Metadata publishers are removed (lines 760-761)\\n4.
